This is currently called from the 'main' thread, which also\n   137→// handles 'push' requests and close - the code will eventually call the 'push' code, and it needs more mutex\n   138→// protection. Original code avoided the mutexes by doing both 'push' and 'process requests' in same thread.\n   139→func (s *DiscoveryServer) processRequest(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest, con *Connection) error {\n   140→\tstype := v3.GetShortType(req.TypeUrl)\n   141→\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s resources:%d nonce:%s version:%s \", stype,\n   142→\t\tcon.ID(), len(req.ResourceNames), req.ResponseNonce, req.VersionInfo)\n   143→\tif req.TypeUrl == v3.HealthInfoType {\n   144→\t\ts.handleWorkloadHealthcheck(con.proxy, req)\n   145→\t\treturn nil\n   146→\t}\n   147→\n   148→\t// For now, don't let xDS piggyback debug requests start watchers.\n   149→\tif strings.HasPrefix(req.TypeUrl, v3.DebugType) {\n   150→\t\treturn s.pushXds(con,\n   151→\t\t\t&model.WatchedResource{TypeUrl: req.TypeUrl, ResourceNames: sets.New(req.ResourceNames...)},\n   152→\t\t\t&model.PushRequest{Full: true, Push: con.proxy.LastPushContext, Forced: true})\n   153→\t}\n   154→\n   155→\tshouldRespond, delta := xds.ShouldRespond(con.proxy, con.ID(), req)\n   156→\tif !shouldRespond {\n   157→\t\treturn nil\n   158→\t}\n   159→\n   160→\trequest := &model.PushRequest{\n   161→\t\tFull:   true,\n   162→\t\tPush:   con.proxy.LastPushContext,\n   163→\t\tReason: model.NewReasonStats(model.ProxyRequest),\n   164→\n   165→\t\t// The usage of LastPushTime (rather than time.Now()), is critical here for correctness; This time\n   166→\t\t// is used by the XDS cache to determine if a entry is stale. If we use Now() with an old push context,\n   167→\t\t// we may end up overriding active cache entries with stale ones.\n   168→\t\tStart:  con.proxy.LastPushTime,\n   169→\t\tDelta:  delta,\n   170→\t\tForced: true,\n   171→\t}\n   172→\n   173→\t// SidecarScope for the proxy may not have been updated based on this pushContext.\n   174→\t// It can happen when `processRequest` comes after push context has been updated(s.initPushContext),\n   175→\t// but proxy's SidecarScope has been updated(s.computeProxyState -> SetSidecarScope) due to optimizations that skip sidecar scope\n   176→\t// computation.\n   177→\tif con.proxy.SidecarScope != nil && con.proxy.SidecarScope.Version != request.Push.PushVersion {\n   178→\t\ts.computeProxyState(con.proxy, request)\n   179→\t}\n   180→\treturn s.pushXds(con, con.proxy.GetWatchedResource(req.TypeUrl), request)\n   181→}\n   182→\n   183→// StreamAggregatedResources implements the ADS interface.\n   184→func (s *DiscoveryServer) StreamAggregatedResources(stream DiscoveryStream) error {\n   185→\treturn s.Stream(stream)\n   186→}\n   187→\n   188→func (s *DiscoveryServer) Stream(stream DiscoveryStream) error {\n   189→\tif knativeEnv != \"\" && firstRequest.Load() {\n   190→\t\t// How scaling works in knative is the first request is the \"loading\" request. During\n   191→\t\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\n   192→\t\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. As a\n   193→\t\t// result, we should exit the first request immediately; clients will retry.\n   194→\t\tfirstRequest.Store(false)\n   195→\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server warmup not complete; try again\")\n   196→\t}\n   197→\t// Check if server is ready to accept clients and process new requests.\n   198→\t// Currently ready means caches have been synced and hence can build\n   199→\t// clusters correctly. Without this check, InitContext() call below would\n   200→\t// initialize with empty config, leading to reconnected Envoys losing\n   201→\t// configuration. This is an additional safety check inaddition to adding\n   202→\t// cachesSynced logic to readiness probe to handle cases where kube-proxy\n   203→\t// ip tables update latencies.\n   204→\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495.\n   205→\tif !s.IsServerReady() {\n   206→\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server is not ready to serve discovery information\")\n   207→\t}\n   208→\n   209→\tctx := stream.Context()\n   210→\tpeerAddr := \"0.0.0.0\"\n   211→\tif peerInfo, ok := peer.FromContext(ctx); ok {\n   212→\t\tpeerAddr = peerInfo.Addr.String()\n   213→\t}\n   214→\n   215→\tif err := s.WaitForRequestLimit(stream.Context()); err != nil {\n   216→\t\tlog.Warnf(\"ADS: %q exceeded rate limit: %v\", peerAddr, err)\n   217→\t\treturn status.Errorf(codes.ResourceExhausted, \"request rate limit exceeded: %v\", err)\n   218→\t}\n   219→\n   220→\tids, err := s.authenticate(ctx)\n   221→\tif err != nil {\n   222→\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated, err.Error())\n   223→\t}\n   224→\tif ids != nil {\n   225→\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Authenticated XDS: %v with identity %v\", peerAddr, ids)\n   226→\t} else {\n   227→\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Unauthenticated XDS: %s\", peerAddr)\n   228→\t}\n   229→\n   230→\t// InitContext returns immediately if the context was already initialized.\n   231→\ts.globalPushContext().InitContext(s.Env, nil, nil)\n   232→\tcon := newConnection(peerAddr, stream)\n   233→\tcon.ids = ids\n   234→\tcon.s = s\n   235→\treturn xds.Stream(con)\n   236→}\n   237→\n   238→// update the node associated with the connection, after receiving a packet from envoy, also adds the connection\n   239→// to the tracking map.\n   240→func (s *DiscoveryServer) initConnection(node *core.Node, con *Connection, identities []string) error {\n   241→\t// Setup the initial proxy metadata\n   242→\tproxy, err := s.initProxyMetadata(node)\n   243→\tif err != nil {\n   244→\t\treturn err\n   245→\t}\n   246→\t// Check if proxy cluster has an alias configured, if yes use that as cluster ID for this proxy.\n   247→\tif alias, exists := s.ClusterAliases[proxy.Metadata.ClusterID]; This\n   251→\t// way only new push contexts will be registered for this proxy.\n   252→\tproxy.LastPushContext = s.globalPushContext()\n   253→\t// First request so initialize connection id and start tracking it.\n   254→\tcon.SetID(connectionID(proxy.ID))\n   255→\tcon.node = node\n   256→\tcon.proxy = proxy\n   257→\tif proxy.IsZTunnel() && !features.EnableAmbient {\n   258→\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"ztunnel requires PILOT_ENABLE_AMBIENT=true\")\n   259→\t}\n   260→\n   261→\t// Authorize xds clients\n   262→\tif err := s.authorize(con, identities); err != nil {\n   263→\t\treturn err\n   264→\t}\n   265→\n   266→\t// Register the connection. this allows pushes to be triggered for the proxy. Note: the timing of\n   267→\t// this and initializeProxy important. While registering for pushes *after* initialization is complete seems like\n   268→\t// a better choice, it introduces a race condition; If we complete initialization of a new push\n   269→\t// context between initializeProxy and addCon, we would not get any pushes triggered for the new\n   270→\t// push context, leading the proxy to have a stale state until the next full push.\n   271→\ts.addCon(con.ID(), con)\n   272→\t// Register that initialization is complete. This triggers to calls that it is safe to access the\n   273→\t// proxy\n   274→\tdefer con.MarkInitialized()\n   275→\n   276→\t// Complete full initialization of the proxy\n   277→\tif err := s.initializeProxy(con); err != nil {\n   278→\t\ts.closeConnection(con)\n   279→\t\treturn err\n   280→\t}\n   281→\treturn nil\n   282→}\n   283→\n   284→func (s *DiscoveryServer) closeConnection(con *Connection) {\n   285→\tif con.ID() == \"\" {\n   286→\t\treturn\n   287→\t}\n   288→\ts.removeCon(con.ID())\n   289→\ts.WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect(con)\n   290→}\n   291→\n   292→func connectionID(node string) string {\n   293→\tid := atomic.AddInt64(&connectionNumber, 1)\n   294→\treturn node + \"-\" + strconv.FormatInt(id, 10)\n   295→}\n   296→\n   297→// initProxyMetadata initializes just the basic metadata of a proxy. The service registries have the best access to\n   319→\t// locality information, as they can read from various sources (Node on Kubernetes, for example). They will take this\n   320→\t// information and add it to the labels. So while the proxy may not originally have these labels,\n   321→\t// it will by the time we get here (as a result of calling this after SetWorkloadLabels).\n   322→\tproxy.Locality = localityFromProxyLabels(proxy)\n   323→\tif proxy.Locality == nil {\n   324→\t\t// If there is no locality in the registry then use the one sent as part of the discovery request.\n   325→\t\t// This is not preferable as only the connected Pilot is aware of this proxies location, but it\n   326→\t\t// can still help provide some client-side Envoy context when load balancing based on location.\n   327→\t\tproxy.Locality = &core.Locality{\n   328→\t\t\tRegion:  proxy.XdsNode.Locality.GetRegion(),\n   329→\t\t\tZone:    proxy.XdsNode.Locality.GetZone(),\n   330→\t\t\tSubZone: proxy.XdsNode.Locality.GetSubZone(),\n   331→\t\t}\n   332→\t}\n   333→\t// add topology labels to proxy labels\n   334→\tproxy.Labels = labelutil.AugmentLabels(\n   335→\t\tproxy.Labels,\n   336→\t\tproxy.Metadata.ClusterID,\n   337→\t\tutil.LocalityToString(proxy.Locality),\n   338→\t\tproxy.GetNodeName(),\n   339→\t\tproxy.Metadata.Network,\n   340→\t)\n   341→}\n   342→\n   343→func localityFromProxyLabels(proxy *model.Proxy) *core.Locality {\n   344→\tregion, f1 := proxy.Labels[labelutil.LabelTopologyRegion]\n   345→\tzone, f2 := proxy.Labels[labelutil.LabelTopologyZone]\n   346→\tsubzone, f3 := proxy.Labels[label.TopologySubzone.Name]\n   347→\tif !f1 && !f2 && !f3 {\n   348→\t\t// If no labels set, we didn't find the locality from the service registry. We do support a (mostly undocumented/internal)\n   349→\t\t// label to override the locality, so respect that here as well.\n   350→\t\tlocalityLabel := pm.GetLocalityLabel(proxy.Labels)\n   351→\t\tif localityLabel != \"\" {\n   352→\t\t\treturn util.ConvertLocality(localityLabel)\n   353→\t\t}\n   354→\t\treturn nil\n   355→\t}\n   356→\treturn &core.Locality{\n   357→\t\tRegion:  region,\n   358→\t\tZone:    zone,\n   359→\t\tSubZone: subzone,\n   360→\t}\n   361→}\n   362→\n   363→// initializeProxy completes the initialization of a proxy. Though this might be redundant sometimes, we still\n   409→\t// have to compute this because as part of a config change, a new Sidecar could become\n   410→\t// applicable to this proxy\n   411→\tpush := proxy.LastPushContext\n   412→\tif request == nil {\n   413→\t\tshouldResetSidecarScope = true\n   414→\t} else {\n   415→\t\tpush = request.Push\n   416→\t\tif request.Forced {\n   417→\t\t\tshouldResetSidecarScope = true\n   418→\t\t}\n   419→\t\tfor conf := range request.ConfigsUpdated {\n   420→\t\t\tswitch conf.Kind {\n   421→\t\t\tcase kind.ServiceEntry, kind.DestinationRule, kind.VirtualService, kind.Sidecar:\n   422→\t\t\t\tshouldResetSidecarScope = true\n   423→\t\t\tcase kind.Gateway:\n   424→\t\t\t\tshouldResetGateway = true\n   425→\t\t\tcase 430→\t\t\t\tbreak\n   431→\t\t\t}\n   432→\t\t}\n   433→\t}\n   434→\t// compute the sidecarscope for both proxy type whenever it changes.\n   435→\tif shouldResetSidecarScope {\n   436→\t\tproxy.SetSidecarScope(push)\n   437→\t}\n   438→\t// only compute gateways for \"router\" type proxy.\n   439→\tif shouldResetGateway && proxy.Type == model.Router {\n   440→\t\tproxy.SetGatewaysForProxy(push)\n   441→\t}\n   442→\tproxy.LastPushContext = push\n   443→\tif request != nil {\n   444→\t\tproxy.LastPushTime = request.Start\n   445→\t}\n   446→}\n   447→\n event.\n   582→func (s *DiscoveryServer) StartPush(req *model.PushRequest) {\n   583→\t// Push config changes, iterating over connected envoys.\n   584→\tif log.DebugEnabled() {\n   585→\t\tcurrentlyPending := s.pushQueue.Pending()\n   586→\t\tif currentlyPending != 0 {\n   587→\t\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Starting new push while %v were still pending\", currentlyPending)\n   588→\t\t}\n 609→\t\txds.TotalXDSInternalErrors.Increment()\n   610→\t} else {\n   611→\t\tdelete(s.adsClients, conID)\n   612→\t\trecordXDSClients(con.proxy.Metadata.IstioVersion, -1)\n   613→\t}\n   614→}\n connection.\n\tconnectionNumber = int64(0)\n)\n\n// Used only when running in KNative, to handle the load balancing behavior.\nvar firstRequest = uatomic.NewBool(true)\n\nvar knativeEnv = env.Register(\"K_REVISION\", \"\",\n\t\"KNative revision, set if running in knative\").Get()\n\n// DiscoveryStream is a server interface for XDS.\ntype DiscoveryStream = xds.DiscoveryStream\n\n// discovery.AggregatedDiscoveryService_DeltaAggregatedResourcesClient\n\ntype Connection struct {\n\txds.Connection\n\n\t// Original node metadata, to avoid unmarshal/marshal.\n\t// This is included in internal events.\n\tnode *core.Node\n\n\t// proxy is the client to which this connection is established.\n\tproxy *model.Proxy\n\n\t// deltaStream is used for Delta XDS. Only one of deltaStream or stream will be set\n\tdeltaStream DeltaDiscoveryStream\n\n\tdeltaReqChan chan *discovery.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\n\n\ts   *DiscoveryServer\n\tids []string\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) XdsConnection() *xds.Connection {\n\treturn &conn.Connection\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Proxy() *model.Proxy {\n\treturn conn.proxy\n}\n\n// Event represents a config or registry event that results in a push.\ntype Event struct {\n\t// pushRequest PushRequest to use for the push.\n\tpushRequest *model.PushRequest\n\n\t// function to call once a push is finished. This must be called or future changes may be blocked.\n\tdone func()\n}\n\nfunc newConnection(peerAddr string, stream DiscoveryStream) *Connection {\n\treturn &Connection{\n\t\tConnection: xds.NewConnection(peerAddr, stream),\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Initialize(node *core.Node) error {\n\treturn conn.s.initConnection(node, conn, conn.ids)\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Close() {\n\tconn.s.closeConnection(conn)\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Watcher() xds.Watcher {\n\treturn conn.proxy\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Process(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) error {\n\treturn conn.s.processRequest(req, conn)\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Push(ev any) error {\n\tpushEv := ev.(*Event)\n\terr := conn.s.pushConnection(conn, pushEv)\n\tpushEv.done()\n\treturn err\n}\n\n// processRequest handles one discovery request. This is currently called from the 'main' thread, which also\n// handles 'push' requests and close - the code will eventually call the 'push' code, and it needs more mutex\n// protection. Original code avoided the mutexes by doing both 'push' and 'process requests' in same thread.\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) processRequest(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest, con *Connection) error {\n\tstype := v3.GetShortType(req.TypeUrl)\n\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s resources:%d nonce:%s version:%s \", stype,\n\t\tcon.ID(), len(req.ResourceNames), req.ResponseNonce, req.VersionInfo)\n\tif req.TypeUrl == v3.HealthInfoType {\n\t\ts.handleWorkloadHealthcheck(con.proxy, req)\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\t// For now, don't let xDS piggyback debug requests start watchers.\n\tif strings.HasPrefix(req.TypeUrl, v3.DebugType) {\n\t\treturn s.pushXds(con,\n\t\t\t&model.WatchedResource{TypeUrl: req.TypeUrl, ResourceNames: sets.New(req.ResourceNames...)},\n\t\t\t&model.PushRequest{Full: true, Push: con.proxy.LastPushContext, Forced: true})\n\t}\n\n\tshouldRespond, delta := xds.ShouldRespond(con.proxy, con.ID(), req)\n\tif !shouldRespond {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\trequest := &model.PushRequest{\n\t\tFull:   true,\n\t\tPush:   con.proxy.LastPushContext,\n\t\tReason: model.NewReasonStats(model.ProxyRequest),\n\n\t\t// The usage of LastPushTime (rather than time.Now()), is critical here for correctness; This time\n\t\t// is used by the XDS cache to determine if a entry is stale. If we use Now() with an old push context,\n\t\t// we may end up overriding active cache entries with stale ones.\n\t\tStart:  con.proxy.LastPushTime,\n\t\tDelta:  delta,\n\t\tForced: true,\n\t}\n\n\t// SidecarScope for the proxy may not have been updated based on this pushContext.\n\t// It can happen when `processRequest` comes after push context has been updated(s.initPushContext),\n\t// but proxy's SidecarScope has been updated(s.computeProxyState -> SetSidecarScope) due to optimizations that skip sidecar scope\n\t// computation.\n\tif con.proxy.SidecarScope != nil && con.proxy.SidecarScope.Version != request.Push.PushVersion {\n\t\ts.computeProxyState(con.proxy, request)\n\t}\n\treturn s.pushXds(con, con.proxy.GetWatchedResource(req.TypeUrl), request)\n}\n\n// StreamAggregatedResources implements the ADS interface.\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) StreamAggregatedResources(stream DiscoveryStream) error {\n\treturn s.Stream(stream)\n}\n\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) Stream(stream DiscoveryStream) error {\n\tif knativeEnv != \"\" && firstRequest.Load() {\n\t\t// How scaling works in knative is the first request is the \"loading\" request. During\n\t\t// loading request, concurrency=1. Once that request is done, concurrency is enabled.\n\t\t// However, the XDS stream is long lived, so the first request would block all others. As a\n\t\t// result, we should exit the first request immediately; clients will retry.\n\t\tfirstRequest.Store(false)\n\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server warmup not complete; try again\")\n\t}\n\t// Check if server is ready to accept clients and process new requests.\n\t// Currently ready means caches have been synced and hence can build\n\t// clusters correctly. Without this check, InitContext() call below would\n\t// initialize with empty config, leading to reconnected Envoys losing\n\t// configuration. This is an additional safety check inaddition to adding\n\t// cachesSynced logic to readiness probe to handle cases where kube-proxy\n\t// ip tables update latencies.\n\t// See https://github.com/istio/istio/issues/25495.\n\tif !s.IsServerReady() {\n\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unavailable, \"server is not ready to serve discovery information\")\n\t}\n\n\tctx := stream.Context()\n\tpeerAddr := \"0.0.0.0\"\n\tif peerInfo, ok := peer.FromContext(ctx); ok {\n\t\tpeerAddr = peerInfo.Addr.String()\n\t}\n\n\tif err := s.WaitForRequestLimit(stream.Context()); err != nil {\n\t\tlog.Warnf(\"ADS: %q exceeded rate limit: %v\", peerAddr, err)\n\t\treturn status.Errorf(codes.ResourceExhausted, \"request rate limit exceeded: %v\", err)\n\t}\n\n\tids, err := s.authenticate(ctx)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated, err.Error())\n\t}\n\tif ids != nil {\n\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Authenticated XDS: %v with identity %v\", peerAddr, ids)\n\t} else {\n\t\tlog.Debugf(\"Unauthenticated XDS: %s\", peerAddr)\n\t}\n\n\t// InitContext returns immediately if the context was already initialized.\n\ts.globalPushContext().InitContext(s.Env, nil, nil)\n\tcon := newConnection(peerAddr, stream)\n\tcon.ids = ids\n\tcon.s = s\n\treturn xds.Stream(con)\n}\n\n// update the node associated with the connection, after receiving a packet from envoy, also adds the connection\n// to the tracking map.\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) initConnection(node *core.Node, con *Connection, identities []string) error {\n\t// Setup the initial proxy metadata\n\tproxy, err := s.initProxyMetadata(node)\n\tif err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\t// Check if proxy cluster has an alias configured, if yes use that as cluster ID for this proxy.\n\tif alias, exists := s.ClusterAliases[proxy.Metadata.ClusterID]; exists {\n\t\tproxy.Metadata.ClusterID = alias\n\t}\n\t// To ensure push context is monotonically increasing, setup LastPushContext before we addCon. This\n\t// way only new push contexts will be registered for this proxy.\n\tproxy.LastPushContext = s.globalPushContext()\n\t// First request so initialize connection id and start tracking it.\n\tcon.SetID(connectionID(proxy.ID))\n\tcon.node = node\n\tcon.proxy = proxy\n\tif proxy.IsZTunnel() && !features.EnableAmbient {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"ztunnel requires PILOT_ENABLE_AMBIENT=true\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Authorize xds clients\n\tif err := s.authorize(con, identities); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\n\t// Register the connection. this allows pushes to be triggered for the proxy. Note: the timing of\n\t// this and initializeProxy important. While registering for pushes *after* initialization is complete seems like\n\t// a better choice, it introduces a race condition; If we complete initialization of a new push\n\t// context between initializeProxy and addCon, we would not get any pushes triggered for the new\n\t// push context, leading the proxy to have a stale state until the next full push.\n\ts.addCon(con.ID(), con)\n\t// Register that initialization is complete. This triggers to calls that it is safe to access the\n\t// proxy\n\tdefer con.MarkInitialized()\n\n\t// Complete full initialization of the proxy\n\tif err := s.initializeProxy(con); err != nil {\n\t\ts.closeConnection(con)\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) closeConnection(con *Connection) {\n\tif con.ID() == \"\" {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\ts.removeCon(con.ID())\n\ts.WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect(con)\n}\n\nfunc connectionID(node string) string {\n\tid := atomic.AddInt64(&connectionNumber, 1)\n\treturn node + \"-\" + strconv.FormatInt(id, 10)\n}\n\n// initProxyMetadata initializes just the basic metadata of a proxy. The service registries have the best access to\n\t// locality information, as they can read from various sources (Node on Kubernetes, for example). They will take this\n\t// information and add it to the labels. So while the proxy may not originally have these labels,\n\t// it will by the time we get here (as a result of calling this after SetWorkloadLabels).\n\tproxy.Locality = localityFromProxyLabels(proxy)\n\tif proxy.Locality == nil {\n\t\t// If there is no locality in the registry then use the one sent as part of the discovery request.\n\t\t// This is not preferable as only the connected Pilot is aware of this proxies location, but it\n\t\t// can still help provide some client-side Envoy context when load balancing based on location.\n\t\tproxy.Locality = &core.Locality{\n\t\t\tRegion:  proxy.XdsNode.Locality.GetRegion(),\n\t\t\tZone:    proxy.XdsNode.Locality.GetZone(),\n\t\t\tSubZone: proxy.XdsNode.Locality.GetSubZone(),\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\t// add topology labels to proxy labels\n\tproxy.Labels = labelutil.AugmentLabels(\n\t\tproxy.Labels,\n\t\tproxy.Metadata.ClusterID,\n\t\tutil.LocalityToString(proxy.Locality),\n\t\tproxy.GetNodeName(),\n\t\tproxy.Metadata.Network,\n\t)\n}\n\nfunc localityFromProxyLabels(proxy *model.Proxy) *core.Locality {\n\tregion, f1 := proxy.Labels[labelutil.LabelTopologyRegion]\n\tzone, f2 := proxy.Labels[labelutil.LabelTopologyZone]\n\tsubzone, f3 := proxy.Labels[label.TopologySubzone.Name]\n\tif !f1 && !f2 && !f3 {\n\t\t// If no labels set, we didn't find the locality from the service registry. We do support a (mostly undocumented/internal)\n\t\t// label to override the locality, so respect that here as well.\n\t\tlocalityLabel := pm.GetLocalityLabel(proxy.Labels)\n\t\tif localityLabel != \"\" {\n\t\t\treturn util.ConvertLocality(localityLabel)\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn &core.Locality{\n\t\tRegion:  region,\n\t\tZone:    zone,\n\t\tSubZone: subzone,\n\t}\n}\n\n// initializeProxy completes the initialization of a proxy. It is expected to be called only after\n// initProxyMetadata.\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) initializeProxy(con *Connection) error {\n\tproxy := con.proxy\n\t// this should be done before we look for service instances, but after we load metadata\n\t// TODO fix check in kubecontroller treat echo VMs like there isn't a pod\n\tif err := s.WorkloadEntryController.OnConnect(con); err != nil {\n\t\treturn err\n\t}\n\ts.computeProxyState(proxy, nil)\n\t// Discover supported IP Versions of proxy so that appropriate config can be delivered.\n\tproxy.DiscoverIPMode()\n\n\tproxy.WatchedResources = map[string]*model.WatchedResource{}\n\t// Based on node metadata and version, we can associate a different generator.\n\tif proxy.Metadata.Generator != \"\" {\n\t\tproxy.XdsResourceGenerator = s.Generators[proxy.Metadata.Generator]\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) computeProxyState(proxy *model.Proxy, request *model.PushRequest) {\n\tproxy.Lock()\n\tdefer proxy.Unlock()\n\tvar shouldResetGateway, shouldResetSidecarScope bool\n\t// 1. If request == nil(initiation phase) or request.ConfigsUpdated == nil(global push), set proxy serviceTargets.\n\t// 2. otherwise only set when svc update, this is for the case that a service may select the proxy\n\tif request == nil || request.Forced ||\n\t\tproxy.ShouldUpdateServiceTargets(request.ConfigsUpdated) {\n\t\tproxy.SetServiceTargets(s.Env.ServiceDiscovery)\n\t\t// proxy.SetGatewaysForProxy depends on the serviceTargets,\n\t\t// so when we reset serviceTargets, should reset gateway as well.\n\t\tshouldResetGateway = true\n\t}\n\n\t// only recompute workload labels when\n\t// 1. stream established and proxy first time initialization\n\t// 2. proxy update\n\trecomputeLabels := request == nil || request.IsProxyUpdate()\n\tif recomputeLabels {\n\t\tproxy.SetWorkloadLabels(s.Env)\n\t\tsetTopologyLabels(proxy)\n\t}\n\t// Precompute the sidecar scope and merged gateways associated with this proxy.\n\t// Saves compute cycles in networking code. conn.stream.Context().Done()\n   194→}\n   195→\n   196→func (conn *Connection) ID() string {\n   197→\treturn conn.conID\n   198→}\n   199→\n   200→func (conn *Connection) Peer() string {\n   201→\treturn conn.peerAddr\n   202→}\n   203→\n   204→func (conn *Connection) SetID(id string) {\n   205→\tconn.conID = id\n   206→}\n   207→\n   208→func (conn *Connection) ConnectedAt() time.Time {\n   209→\treturn conn.connectedAt\n   210→}\n   211→\n   212→func (conn *Connection) Stop() {\n   213→\tclose(conn.stop)\n   214→}\n   215→\n   216→func (conn *Connection) MarkInitialized() {\n   217→\tclose(conn.initialized)\n   218→}\n   219→\n   220→// ConnectionContext is used by the RPC event loop to respond to requests and pushes.\n   221→type ConnectionContext interface {\n   222→\tXdsConnection() *Connection\n   223→\tWatcher() Watcher\n   224→\t// Initialize checks the first request.\n   225→\tInitialize(node *core.Node) error\n   226→\t// Close discards the connection.\n   227→\tClose()\n   228→\t// Process responds to a discovery request.\n   229→\tProcess(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) error\n   230→\t// Push responds to a push event queue\n   231→\tPush(ev any) error\n   232→}\n   233→\n   234→func Stream(ctx ConnectionContext) error {\n   235→\tcon := ctx.XdsConnection()\n   236→\t// Do not call: defer close(con.pushChannel). The push channel will be garbage collected\n   237→\t// when the connection is no longer used. Closing the channel can cause subtle race conditions\n   238→\t// with push. According to the spec: \"It's only necessary to close a channel when it is important\n   239→\t// to tell the receiving goroutines that all data have been sent.\"\n   240→\n   241→\t// Block until either a request is received or a push is triggered.\n   242→\t// We need 2 go routines because 'read' blocks in Recv().\n   243→\tgo Receive(ctx)\n   244→\n   245→\t// Wait for the proxy to be fully initialized before we start serving traffic. Because\n   246→\t// initialization doesn't have dependencies that will block, there is no need to add any timeout\n   247→\t// here. Prior to this explicit wait, we were implicitly waiting by receive() not sending to\n   248→\t// reqChannel and the connection not being enqueued for pushes to pushChannel until the\n   249→\t// initialization is complete.\n   250→\t<-con.initialized\n   251→\n   252→\tfor {\n   253→\t\t// Go select{} statements are not ordered; the same channel can be chosen many times.\n   254→\t\t// For requests, these are higher priority (client may be blocked on startup until these are done)\n   255→\t\t// and often very cheap to handle (simple ACK), so we check it first.\n   256→\t\tselect {\n   257→\t\tcase req, ok := <-con.reqChan:\n   258→\t\t\tif ok {\n   259→\t\t\t\tif err := ctx.Process(req); err != nil {\n   260→\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n   261→\t\t\t\t}\n   262→\t\t\t} else {\n   263→\t\t\t\t// Remote side closed connection or error processing the request.\n   264→\t\t\t\treturn <-con.errorChan\n   265→\t\t\t}\n   266→\t\tcase <-con.stop:\n   267→\t\t\treturn nil\n   268→\t\tdefault:\n   269→\t\t}\n   270→\t\t// If there wasn't already a request, poll for requests and pushes. Note: if we have a huge\n   271→\t\t// amount of incoming requests, we may still send some pushes, as we do not `continue` above;\n   272→\t\t// however, requests will be handled ~2x as much as pushes. This ensures a wave of requests\n   273→\t\t// cannot completely starve pushes. However, this scenario is unlikely.\n   274→\t\tselect {\n   275→\t\tcase req, ok := <-con.reqChan:\n   276→\t\t\tif ok {\n   277→\t\t\t\tif err := ctx.Process(req); err != nil {\n   278→\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n   279→\t\t\t\t}\n   280→\t\t\t} else {\n   281→\t\t\t\t// Remote side closed connection or error processing the request.\n   282→\t\t\t\treturn <-con.errorChan\n   283→\t\t\t}\n   284→\t\tcase pushEv := <-con.pushChannel:\n   285→\t\t\terr := ctx.Push(pushEv)\n   286→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   287→\t\t\t\treturn err\n   288→\t\t\t}\n   289→\t\tcase <-con.stop:\n   290→\t\t\treturn nil\n   291→\t\t}\n   292→\t}\n   293→}\n   294→\n   295→func Receive(ctx ConnectionContext) {\n   296→\tcon := ctx.XdsConnection()\n   297→\tdefer func() {\n   298→\t\tclose(con.errorChan)\n   299→\t\tclose(con.reqChan)\n   300→\t\t// Close the initialized channel, if its not already closed, to prevent blocking the stream.\n   301→\t\tselect {\n   302→\t\tcase <-con.initialized:\n   303→\t\tdefault:\n   304→\t\t\tclose(con.initialized)\n   305→\t\t}\n   306→\t}()\n   307→\n   308→\tfirstRequest := true\n   309→\tfor {\n   310→\t\treq, err := con.stream.Recv()\n   311→\t\tif err != nil {\n   312→\t\t\tif istiogrpc.GRPCErrorType(err) != istiogrpc.UnexpectedError {\n   313→\t\t\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS: %q %s terminated\", con.peerAddr, con.conID)\n   314→\t\t\t\treturn\n   315→\t\t\t}\n   316→\t\t\tcon.errorChan <- err\n   317→\t\t\tlog.Errorf(\"ADS: %q %s terminated with error: %v\", con.peerAddr, con.conID, err)\n   318→\t\t\tTotalXDSInternalErrors.Increment()\n   319→\t\t\treturn\n   320→\t\t}\n   321→\t\t// This should be only set for the first request. The node id may not be set - for example malicious clients.\n   322→\t\tif firstRequest {\n   323→\t\t\t// probe happens before envoy sends first xDS request\n   324→\t\t\tif req.TypeUrl == model.HealthInfoType {\n   325→\t\t\t\tlog.Warnf(\"ADS: %q %s send health check probe before normal xDS request\", con.peerAddr, con.conID)\n   326→\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   327→\t\t\t}\n   328→\t\t\tfirstRequest = false\n   329→\t\t\tif req.Node == nil || req.Node.Id == \"\" {\n   330→\t\t\t\tcon.errorChan <- status.New(codes.InvalidArgument, \"missing node information\").Err()\n   331→\t\t\t\treturn\n   332→\t\t\t}\n   333→\t\t\tif err := ctx.Initialize(req.Node); err != nil {\n   334→\t\t\t\tcon.errorChan <- err\n   335→\t\t\t\treturn\n   336→\t\t\t}\n   337→\t\t\tdefer ctx.Close()\n   338→\t\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS: new connection for node:%s\", con.conID)\n   339→\t\t}\n   340→\n   341→\t\tselect {\n   342→\t\tcase con.reqChan <- req:\n   343→\t\tcase <-con.stream.Context().Done():\n   344→\t\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS: %q %s terminated with stream closed\", con.peerAddr, con.conID)\n   345→\t\t\treturn\n   346→\t\t}\n   347→\t}\n   348→}\n   349→\n   350→// ShouldRespond determines whether this request needs to be responded back. It applies the ack/nack rules as per xds protocol\n   351→// using WatchedResource for previous state and discovery request for the current state.\n   352→func ShouldRespond(w Watcher, id string, request *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) (bool, ResourceDelta) {\n   353→\tstype := model.GetShortType(request.TypeUrl)\n   354→\n   355→\t// If there is an error in request that means previous response is erroneous.\n   356→\t// We do not have to respond in that case. In this case request's version info\n   357→\t// will be different from the version sent. But it is fragile to rely on that.\n   358→\tif request.ErrorDetail != nil {\n   359→\t\terrCode := codes.Code(request.ErrorDetail.Code)\n   360→\t\tlog.Warnf(\"ADS:%s: ACK ERROR %s %s:%s\", stype, id, errCode.String(), request.ErrorDetail.GetMessage())\n   361→\t\tIncrementXDSRejects(request.TypeUrl, w.GetID(), errCode.String())\n   362→\t\tw.UpdateWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl, func(wr *WatchedResource) *WatchedResource {\n   363→\t\t\twr.LastError = request.ErrorDetail.GetMessage()\n   364→\t\t\treturn wr\n   365→\t\t})\n   366→\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n   367→\t}\n   368→\n   369→\tif shouldUnsubscribe(request) {\n   370→\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: UNSUBSCRIBE %s %s %s\", stype, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n   371→\t\tw.DeleteWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl)\n   372→\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n   373→\t}\n   374→\n   375→\tpreviousInfo := w.GetWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl)\n   376→\t// This can happen in two cases:\n   377→\t// 1. When Envoy starts for the first time, it sends an initial Discovery request to Istiod.\n   378→\t// 2. When Envoy reconnects to a new Istiod that does not have information about this typeUrl\n   379→\t// i.e. non empty response nonce.\n   380→\t// We should always respond with the current resource names.\n   381→\tif request.ResponseNonce == \"\" || previousInfo == nil {\n   382→\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: INIT/RECONNECT %s %s %s\", stype, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n   383→\t\tw.NewWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl, request.ResourceNames)\n   384→\t\treturn true, emptyResourceDelta\n   385→\t}\n   386→\n   387→\t// If there is mismatch in the nonce, that is a case of expired/stale nonce.\n   388→\t// A nonce becomes stale following a newer nonce being sent to Envoy.\n   389→\t// previousInfo.NonceSent can be empty if we previously had shouldRespond=true but didn't send any resources.\n   390→\tif request.ResponseNonce != previousInfo.NonceSent {\n   391→\t\tif features.EnableUnsafeAssertions && previousInfo.NonceSent == \"\" {\n   392→\t\t\t// Assert we do not end up in an invalid state\n   393→\t\t\tlog.Fatalf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s Expired nonce received %s, but we never sent any nonce\", stype,\n   394→\t\t\t\tid, request.ResponseNonce)\n   395→\t\t}\n   396→\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s Expired nonce received %s, sent %s\", stype,\n   397→\t\t\tid, request.ResponseNonce, previousInfo.NonceSent)\n   398→\t\tExpiredNonce.With(typeTag.Value(model.GetMetricType(request.TypeUrl))).Increment()\n   399→\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n   400→\t}\n   401→\n   402→\t// If it comes here, that means nonce match.\n   403→\tvar previousResources sets.String\n   404→\tvar cur sets.String\n   405→\tvar alwaysRespond bool\n   406→\tw.UpdateWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl, func(wr *WatchedResource) *WatchedResource {\n   407→\t\t// Clear last error, we got an ACK.\n   408→\t\twr.LastError = \"\"\n   409→\t\tpreviousResources = wr.ResourceNames\n   410→\t\twr.NonceAcked = request.ResponseNonce\n   411→\t\twr.ResourceNames = sets.New(request.ResourceNames...)\n   412→\t\tcur = wr.ResourceNames\n   413→\t\talwaysRespond = wr.AlwaysRespond\n   414→\t\twr.AlwaysRespond = false\n   415→\t\treturn wr\n   416→\t})\n   417→\n   418→\t// Envoy can send two DiscoveryRequests with same version and nonce.\n   419→\t// when it detects a new resource. We should respond if they change.\n   420→\tremoved := previousResources.Difference(cur)\n   421→\tadded := cur.Difference(previousResources)\n   422→\n   423→\t// We should always respond \"alwaysRespond\" marked requests to let Envoy finish warming\n   424→\t// even though Nonce match and it looks like an ACK.\n   425→\tif alwaysRespond {\n   426→\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS:%s: FORCE RESPONSE %s for warming.\", stype, id)\n   427→\t\treturn true, emptyResourceDelta\n   428→\t}\n   429→\n   430→\tif len(removed) == 0 && len(added) == 0 {\n   431→\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: ACK %s %s %s\", stype, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n   432→\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n   433→\t}\n   434→\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: RESOURCE CHANGE added %v removed %v %s %s %s\", stype,\n   435→\t\tadded, removed, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n   436→\n   437→\t// For non wildcard resource, if no new resources are subscribed, it means we do not need to push.\n   438→\tif !IsWildcardTypeURL(request.TypeUrl) && len(added) == 0 {\n   439→\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n   440→\t}\n   441→\n   442→\treturn true, ResourceDelta{\n   443→\t\tSubscribed: added,\n   444→\t\t// we do not need to set unsubscribed for StoW\n   445→\t}\n   446→}\n   447→\n   448→// shouldUnsubscribe checks if we should unsubscribe. This is done when Envoy is\n   449→// no longer watching. For example, we remove all RDS references, we will\n   450→// unsubscribe from RDS. NOTE: This may happen as part of the initial request. If\n   451→// there are no routes needed, Envoy will send an empty request, which this\n   452→// properly handles by not adding it to the watched resource list.\n   453→func shouldUnsubscribe(request *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) bool {\n   454→\treturn len(request.ResourceNames) == 0 && !IsWildcardTypeURL(request.TypeUrl)\n   455→}\n   456→\n   457→func Send(ctx ConnectionContext, res *discovery.DiscoveryResponse) error {\n   458→\tconn := ctx.XdsConnection()\n   459→\tsendResponse := func() error {\n   460→\t\tstart := time.Now()\n   461→\t\tdefer func() { RecordSendTime(time.Since(start)) }()\n   462→\t\treturn conn.stream.Send(res)\n   463→\t}\n   464→\terr := sendResponse()\n   465→\tif err == nil {\n   466→\t\tif res.Nonce != \"\" && !strings.HasPrefix(res.TypeUrl, model.DebugType) {\n   467→\t\t\tctx.Watcher().UpdateWatchedResource(res.TypeUrl, func(wr *WatchedResource) *WatchedResource {\n   468→\t\t\t\tif wr == nil {\n   469→\t\t\t\t\twr = &WatchedResource{TypeUrl: res.TypeUrl}\n   470→\t\t\t\t}\n   471→\t\t\t\twr.NonceSent = res.Nonce\n   472→\t\t\t\twr.LastSendTime = time.Now()\n   473→\t\t\t\treturn wr\n   474→\t\t\t})\n   475→\t\t}\n   476→\t} else if status.Convert(err).Code() == codes.DeadlineExceeded {\n   477→\t\tlog.Infof(\"Timeout writing %s: %v\", conn.conID, model.GetShortType(res.TypeUrl))\n   478→\t\tResponseWriteTimeouts.Increment()\n   479→\t}\n   480→\treturn err\n   481→}\n   482→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/discovery/v3\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/codes\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/grpc/status\"\n\t\"google.golang.org/protobuf/types/known/anypb\"\n\n\t\"istio.io/istio/pilot/pkg/features\"\n\tistiogrpc \"istio.io/istio/pilot/pkg/grpc\"\n\t\"istio.io/istio/pkg/model\"\n\t\"istio.io/istio/pkg/util/sets\"\n)\n\n// ResourceDelta records the difference in requested resources by an XDS client\ntype ResourceDelta struct {\n\t// Subscribed indicates the client requested these additional resources\n\tSubscribed sets.String\n\t// Unsubscribed indicates the client no longer requires these resources\n\tUnsubscribed sets.String\n}\n\nvar emptyResourceDelta = ResourceDelta{}\n\nfunc (rd ResourceDelta) IsEmpty() bool {\n\treturn len(rd.Subscribed) == 0 && len(rd.Unsubscribed) == 0\n}\n\ntype Resources = []*discovery.Resource\n\nfunc ResourcesToAny(r Resources) []*anypb.Any {\n\ta := make([]*anypb.Any, 0, len(r))\n\tfor _, rr := range r {\n\t\ta = append(a, rr.Resource)\n\t}\n\treturn a\n}\n\n// WatchedResource tracks an active DiscoveryRequest subscription.\ntype WatchedResource struct {\n\t// TypeUrl is copied from the DiscoveryRequest.TypeUrl that initiated watching this resource.\n\t// nolint\n\tTypeUrl string\n\n\t// ResourceNames tracks the list of resources that are actively watched.\n\t// For LDS and CDS, all resources of the TypeUrl type are watched if it is empty.\n\t// For endpoints the resource names will have list of clusters and for clusters it is empty.\n\t// For Delta Xds, all resources of the TypeUrl that a client has subscribed to.\n\tResourceNames sets.String\n\n\t// Wildcard indicates the subscription is a wildcard subscription. This only applies to types that\n\t// allow both wildcard and non-wildcard subscriptions.\n\tWildcard bool\n\n\t// NonceSent is the nonce sent in the last sent response. If it is equal with NonceAcked, the\n\t// last message has been processed. If empty: we never sent a message of this type.\n\tNonceSent string\n\n\t// NonceAcked is the last acked message.\n\tNonceAcked string\n\n\t// AlwaysRespond, if true, will ensure that even when a request would otherwise be treated as an\n\t// ACK, it will be responded to. This typically happens when a proxy reconnects to another instance of\n\t// Istiod. In that case, Envoy expects us to respond to EDS/RDS/SDS requests to finish warming of\n\t// clusters/listeners.\n\t// Typically, this should be set to 'false' after response; keeping it true would likely result in an endless loop.\n\tAlwaysRespond bool\n\n\t// LastSendTime tracks the last time we sent a message. This should change every time NonceSent changes.\n\tLastSendTime time.Time\n\n\t// LastError records the last error returned, if any. This is cleared on any successful ACK.\n\tLastError string\n\n\t// LastResources tracks the contents of the last push.\n\t// This field is extremely expensive to maintain and is typically disabled\n\tLastResources Resources\n}\n\ntype Watcher interface {\n\tDeleteWatchedResource(url string)\n\tGetWatchedResource(url string) *WatchedResource\n\tNewWatchedResource(url string, names []string)\n\tUpdateWatchedResource(string, func(*WatchedResource) *WatchedResource)\n\t// GetID identifies an xDS client. This is different from a connection ID.\n\tGetID() string\n}\n\n// IsWildcardTypeURL checks whether a given type is a wildcard type\n// https://www.envoyproxy.io/docs/envoy/latest/api-docs/xds_protocol#how-the-client-specifies-what-resources-to-return\n// If the list of resource names becomes empty, that means that the client is no\n// longer interested in any resources of the specified type. For Listener and\n// Cluster resource types, there is also a “wildcard” mode, which is triggered\n// when the initial request on the stream for that resource type contains no\n// resource names.\nfunc IsWildcardTypeURL(typeURL string) bool {\n\tswitch typeURL {\n\tcase model.SecretType, model.EndpointType, model.RouteType, model.ExtensionConfigurationType:\n\t\t// By XDS spec, these are not wildcard\n\t\treturn false\n\tcase model.ClusterType, model.ListenerType:\n\t\t// By XDS spec, these are wildcard\n\t\treturn true\n\tdefault:\n\t\t// All of our internal types use wildcard semantics\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n}\n\n// DiscoveryStream is a server interface for XDS.\ntype DiscoveryStream = discovery.AggregatedDiscoveryService_StreamAggregatedResourcesServer\n\n// Connection holds information about an xDS client connection. There may be more than one connection to the same client.\ntype Connection struct {\n\t// peerAddr is the address of the client, from network layer.\n\tpeerAddr string\n\n\t// Time of connection, for debugging\n\tconnectedAt time.Time\n\n\t// conID is the connection conID, used as a key in the connection table.\n\t// Currently based on the node name and a counter.\n\tconID string\n\n\t// Sending on this channel results in a push.\n\tpushChannel chan any\n\n\t// Both ADS and SDS streams implement this interface\n\tstream DiscoveryStream\n\n\t// initialized channel will be closed when proxy is initialized. Pushes, or anything accessing\n\t// the proxy, should not be started until this channel is closed.\n\tinitialized chan struct{}\n\n\t// stop can be used to end the connection manually via debug endpoints. Only to be used for testing.\n\tstop chan struct{}\n\n\t// reqChan is used to receive discovery requests for this connection.\n\treqChan chan *discovery.DiscoveryRequest\n\n\t// errorChan is used to process error during discovery request processing.\n\terrorChan chan error\n}\n\nfunc NewConnection(peerAddr string, stream DiscoveryStream) Connection {\n\treturn Connection{\n\t\tpushChannel: make(chan any),\n\t\tinitialized: make(chan struct{}),\n\t\tstop:        make(chan struct{}),\n\t\treqChan:     make(chan *discovery.DiscoveryRequest, 1),\n\t\terrorChan:   make(chan error, 1),\n\t\tpeerAddr:    peerAddr,\n\t\tconnectedAt: time.Now(),\n\t\tstream:      stream,\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) InitializedCh() chan struct{} {\n\treturn conn.initialized\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) PushCh() chan any {\n\treturn conn.pushChannel\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) StopCh() chan struct{} {\n\treturn conn.stop\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) ErrorCh() chan error {\n\treturn conn.errorChan\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) StreamDone() <-chan struct{} {\n\treturn conn.stream.Context().Done()\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) ID() string {\n\treturn conn.conID\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Peer() string {\n\treturn conn.peerAddr\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) SetID(id string) {\n\tconn.conID = id\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) ConnectedAt() time.Time {\n\treturn conn.connectedAt\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) Stop() {\n\tclose(conn.stop)\n}\n\nfunc (conn *Connection) MarkInitialized() {\n\tclose(conn.initialized)\n}\n\n// ConnectionContext is used by the RPC event loop to respond to requests and pushes.\ntype ConnectionContext interface {\n\tXdsConnection() *Connection\n\tWatcher() Watcher\n\t// Initialize checks the first request.\n\tInitialize(node *core.Node) error\n\t// Close discards the connection.\n\tClose()\n\t// Process responds to a discovery request.\n\tProcess(req *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) error\n\t// Push responds to a push event queue\n\tPush(ev any) error\n}\n\nfunc Stream(ctx ConnectionContext) error {\n\tcon := ctx.XdsConnection()\n\t// Do not call: defer close(con.pushChannel). The push channel will be garbage collected\n\t// when the connection is no longer used. Closing the channel can cause subtle race conditions\n\t// with push. According to the spec: \"It's only necessary to close a channel when it is important\n\t// to tell the receiving goroutines that all data have been sent.\"\n\n\t// Block until either a request is received or a push is triggered.\n\t// We need 2 go routines because 'read' blocks in Recv().\n\tgo Receive(ctx)\n\n\t// Wait for the proxy to be fully initialized before we start serving traffic. Because\n\t// initialization doesn't have dependencies that will block, there is no need to add any timeout\n\t// here. Prior to this explicit wait, we were implicitly waiting by receive() not sending to\n\t// reqChannel and the connection not being enqueued for pushes to pushChannel until the\n\t// initialization is complete.\n\t<-con.initialized\n\n\tfor {\n\t\t// Go select{} statements are not ordered; the same channel can be chosen many times.\n\t\t// For requests, these are higher priority (client may be blocked on startup until these are done)\n\t\t// and often very cheap to handle (simple ACK), so we check it first.\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase req, ok := <-con.reqChan:\n\t\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\t\tif err := ctx.Process(req); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// Remote side closed connection or error processing the request.\n\t\t\t\treturn <-con.errorChan\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase <-con.stop:\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t}\n\t\t// If there wasn't already a request, poll for requests and pushes. Note: if we have a huge\n\t\t// amount of incoming requests, we may still send some pushes, as we do not `continue` above;\n\t\t// however, requests will be handled ~2x as much as pushes. This ensures a wave of requests\n\t\t// cannot completely starve pushes. However, this scenario is unlikely.\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase req, ok := <-con.reqChan:\n\t\t\tif ok {\n\t\t\t\tif err := ctx.Process(req); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// Remote side closed connection or error processing the request.\n\t\t\t\treturn <-con.errorChan\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase pushEv := <-con.pushChannel:\n\t\t\terr := ctx.Push(pushEv)\n\t\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase <-con.stop:\n\t\t\treturn nil\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\nfunc Receive(ctx ConnectionContext) {\n\tcon := ctx.XdsConnection()\n\tdefer func() {\n\t\tclose(con.errorChan)\n\t\tclose(con.reqChan)\n\t\t// Close the initialized channel, if its not already closed, to prevent blocking the stream.\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-con.initialized:\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tclose(con.initialized)\n\t\t}\n\t}()\n\n\tfirstRequest := true\n\tfor {\n\t\treq, err := con.stream.Recv()\n\t\tif err != nil {\n\t\t\tif istiogrpc.GRPCErrorType(err) != istiogrpc.UnexpectedError {\n\t\t\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS: %q %s terminated\", con.peerAddr, con.conID)\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tcon.errorChan <- err\n\t\t\tlog.Errorf(\"ADS: %q %s terminated with error: %v\", con.peerAddr, con.conID, err)\n\t\t\tTotalXDSInternalErrors.Increment()\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t\t// This should be only set for the first request. The node id may not be set - for example malicious clients.\n\t\tif firstRequest {\n\t\t\t// probe happens before envoy sends first xDS request\n\t\t\tif req.TypeUrl == model.HealthInfoType {\n\t\t\t\tlog.Warnf(\"ADS: %q %s send health check probe before normal xDS request\", con.peerAddr, con.conID)\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tfirstRequest = false\n\t\t\tif req.Node == nil || req.Node.Id == \"\" {\n\t\t\t\tcon.errorChan <- status.New(codes.InvalidArgument, \"missing node information\").Err()\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tif err := ctx.Initialize(req.Node); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\tcon.errorChan <- err\n\t\t\t\treturn\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tdefer ctx.Close()\n\t\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS: new connection for node:%s\", con.conID)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase con.reqChan <- req:\n\t\tcase <-con.stream.Context().Done():\n\t\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS: %q %s terminated with stream closed\", con.peerAddr, con.conID)\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// ShouldRespond determines whether this request needs to be responded back. It applies the ack/nack rules as per xds protocol\n// using WatchedResource for previous state and discovery request for the current state.\nfunc ShouldRespond(w Watcher, id string, request *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) (bool, ResourceDelta) {\n\tstype := model.GetShortType(request.TypeUrl)\n\n\t// If there is an error in request that means previous response is erroneous.\n\t// We do not have to respond in that case. In this case request's version info\n\t// will be different from the version sent. But it is fragile to rely on that.\n\tif request.ErrorDetail != nil {\n\t\terrCode := codes.Code(request.ErrorDetail.Code)\n\t\tlog.Warnf(\"ADS:%s: ACK ERROR %s %s:%s\", stype, id, errCode.String(), request.ErrorDetail.GetMessage())\n\t\tIncrementXDSRejects(request.TypeUrl, w.GetID(), errCode.String())\n\t\tw.UpdateWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl, func(wr *WatchedResource) *WatchedResource {\n\t\t\twr.LastError = request.ErrorDetail.GetMessage()\n\t\t\treturn wr\n\t\t})\n\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\n\tif shouldUnsubscribe(request) {\n\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: UNSUBSCRIBE %s %s %s\", stype, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n\t\tw.DeleteWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl)\n\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\n\tpreviousInfo := w.GetWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl)\n\t// This can happen in two cases:\n\t// 1. When Envoy starts for the first time, it sends an initial Discovery request to Istiod.\n\t// 2. When Envoy reconnects to a new Istiod that does not have information about this typeUrl\n\t// i.e. non empty response nonce.\n\t// We should always respond with the current resource names.\n\tif request.ResponseNonce == \"\" || previousInfo == nil {\n\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: INIT/RECONNECT %s %s %s\", stype, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n\t\tw.NewWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl, request.ResourceNames)\n\t\treturn true, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\n\t// If there is mismatch in the nonce, that is a case of expired/stale nonce.\n\t// A nonce becomes stale following a newer nonce being sent to Envoy.\n\t// previousInfo.NonceSent can be empty if we previously had shouldRespond=true but didn't send any resources.\n\tif request.ResponseNonce != previousInfo.NonceSent {\n\t\tif features.EnableUnsafeAssertions && previousInfo.NonceSent == \"\" {\n\t\t\t// Assert we do not end up in an invalid state\n\t\t\tlog.Fatalf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s Expired nonce received %s, but we never sent any nonce\", stype,\n\t\t\t\tid, request.ResponseNonce)\n\t\t}\n\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: REQ %s Expired nonce received %s, sent %s\", stype,\n\t\t\tid, request.ResponseNonce, previousInfo.NonceSent)\n\t\tExpiredNonce.With(typeTag.Value(model.GetMetricType(request.TypeUrl))).Increment()\n\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\n\t// If it comes here, that means nonce match.\n\tvar previousResources sets.String\n\tvar cur sets.String\n\tvar alwaysRespond bool\n\tw.UpdateWatchedResource(request.TypeUrl, func(wr *WatchedResource) *WatchedResource {\n\t\t// Clear last error, we got an ACK.\n\t\twr.LastError = \"\"\n\t\tpreviousResources = wr.ResourceNames\n\t\twr.NonceAcked = request.ResponseNonce\n\t\twr.ResourceNames = sets.New(request.ResourceNames...)\n\t\tcur = wr.ResourceNames\n\t\talwaysRespond = wr.AlwaysRespond\n\t\twr.AlwaysRespond = false\n\t\treturn wr\n\t})\n\n\t// Envoy can send two DiscoveryRequests with same version and nonce.\n\t// when it detects a new resource. We should respond if they change.\n\tremoved := previousResources.Difference(cur)\n\tadded := cur.Difference(previousResources)\n\n\t// We should always respond \"alwaysRespond\" marked requests to let Envoy finish warming\n\t// even though Nonce match and it looks like an ACK.\n\tif alwaysRespond {\n\t\tlog.Infof(\"ADS:%s: FORCE RESPONSE %s for warming.\", stype, id)\n\t\treturn true, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\n\tif len(removed) == 0 && len(added) == 0 {\n\t\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: ACK %s %s %s\", stype, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\tlog.Debugf(\"ADS:%s: RESOURCE CHANGE added %v removed %v %s %s %s\", stype,\n\t\tadded, removed, id, request.VersionInfo, request.ResponseNonce)\n\n\t// For non wildcard resource, if no new resources are subscribed, it means we do not need to push.\n\tif !IsWildcardTypeURL(request.TypeUrl) && len(added) == 0 {\n\t\treturn false, emptyResourceDelta\n\t}\n\n\treturn true, ResourceDelta{\n\t\tSubscribed: added,\n\t\t// we do not need to set unsubscribed for StoW\n\t}\n}\n\n// shouldUnsubscribe checks if we should unsubscribe. This is done when Envoy is\n// no longer watching. For example, we remove all RDS references, we will\n// unsubscribe from RDS. NOTE: This may happen as part of the initial request. If\n// there are no routes needed, Envoy will send an empty request, which this\n// properly handles by not adding it to the watched resource list.\nfunc shouldUnsubscribe(request *discovery.DiscoveryRequest) bool {\n\treturn len(request.ResourceNames) == 0 && !IsWildcardTypeURL(request.TypeUrl)\n}\n\nfunc Send(ctx ConnectionContext, res *discovery.DiscoveryResponse) error {\n\tconn := ctx.XdsConnection()\n\tsendResponse := func() error {\n\t\tstart := time.Now()\n\t\tdefer func() { RecordSendTime(time.Since(start)) }()\n\t\treturn conn.stream.Send(res)\n\t}\n\terr := sendResponse()\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\tif res.Nonce != \"\" && !strings.HasPrefix(res.TypeUrl, model.DebugType) {\n\t\t\tctx.Watcher().UpdateWatchedResource(res.TypeUrl, func(wr *WatchedResource) *WatchedResource {\n\t\t\t\tif wr == nil {\n\t\t\t\t\twr = &WatchedResource{TypeUrl: res.TypeUrl}\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\twr.NonceSent = res.Nonce\n\t\t\t\twr.LastSendTime = time.Now()\n\t\t\t\treturn wr\n\t\t\t})\n\t\t}\n\t} else if status.Convert(err).Code() == codes.DeadlineExceeded {\n\t\tlog.Infof(\"Timeout writing %s: %v\", conn.conID, model.GetShortType(res.TypeUrl))\n\t\tResponseWriteTimeouts.Increment()\n\t}\n\treturn err\n}\n","numLines":482,"startLine":1,"totalLines":482}}}
